## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t. The acceleration in such systems typically involves restoring forces (functions of x) and damping forces (functions of v), potentially with nonlinear terms like cubic restoring forces (Duffing oscillator) or nonlinear damping (van der Pol oscillator).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping dependent on position)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Forced oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (harmonic driving force)
- Forced damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity-dependent dissipation)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 * v + c2 * v (mixed nonlinear terms)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric nonlinear restoring force)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear restoring force → term proportional to -x (simple harmonic motion, oscillatory solutions)
- Cubic position terms (x**3) → amplitude-dependent frequency shift characteristic of Duffing-type nonlinearity
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v*(1 - x**2) → self-sustained oscillations (limit cycles, van der Pol type)
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power position terms (x**2) → broken symmetry indicating asymmetric potential wells
- Products of x and v (e.g., x*v, x**2*v) → energy-dependent damping or nonlinear phase-space coupling
- Sinusoidal functions of position sin(c*x) → pendulum-like dynamics with multiple equilibria
- Explicit time dependence via trigonometric functions → external periodic forcing or parametric excitation
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system (energy conservation or dissipation governs dynamics)
- Velocity terms with odd powers (v, v**3) → dissipative forces preserving time-reversal symmetry structure

log ≠ polynomial in v.

### Candidate 43: (c0*v+c1 + (c2*v+c3)*(c4*x+c5+c6*sin(t)*cos(c7*x)))/(c2*v+c3)
= (c0*v+c1)/(c2*v+c3) + c4*x + c5 + c6*sin(t)*cos(c7*x). The first term is a rational function of v. Setting c0=c2*k and c1=c3*k makes it constant k. So: k + c4*x + c5 + c6*sin(t)*cos(c7*x) = const + c4*x + c6*sin(t)*cos(c7*x). No v dependence at all (besides the constant absorbed). Missing v, v*sin(x), v³.

Wait, let me reconsider. If c0 ≠ c2*k for some k, then (c0*v+c1)/(c2*v+c3) is a Möbius transform in v, which can't produce v*sin(x) + v³.
Candidate 43 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 53: c0*x + c1 + c2*sin(c3+t)*cos(c4*x) + c5*v + c6*v³
Set c0=0, c1=0. Then: c2*sin(c3+t)*cos(c4*x) + c5*v + c6*v³. 

GT = 0.3837*sin(t) - 0.6577*v*sin(x) - 1.3155*v - 0.0313*v³

This candidate has sin(t+c3)*cos(c4*x), v, and v³. But GT has sin(t) (no x dependence in that term) and v*sin(x). 

The term c2*sin(c3+t)*cos(c4*x): if c4=0, this becomes c2*sin(c3+t) = sin(t) with phase shift. That gives sin(t) + v + v³. But then we're missing v*sin(x).

Can sin(c3+t)*cos(c4*x) with c4≠0 produce both sin(t) and v*sin(x)? No - it doesn't involve v at all. So we can't get v*sin(x) from this candidate.
